Abstract	O
This	O
study	O
reports	O
the	O
1st	O
conclusive	O
evidence	O
of	O
zoonotic	O
camelpox	B-Virus
virus	O
(	O
CMLV	O
)	O
infection	O
in	O
humans	O
associated	O
with	O
outbreaks	O
in	O
dromedarian	O
camels	O
(	O
_Camelus	O
dromedaries_	O
)	O
in	O
the	O
northwest	O
region	O
of	O
India	B-Country
during	O
2009	O
.	O

CMLV	O
infection	O
is	O
usually	O
restricted	O
to	O
camels	O
and	O
causes	O
localised	O
skin	O
lesions	O
but	O
occasionally	O
leads	O
to	O
a	O
generalised	O
form	O
of	O
disease	O
.	O

However	O
,	O
the	O
present	O
outbreak	O
involved	O
camel	O
handlers	O
and	O
attendants	O
,	O
with	O
clinical	O
manifestations	O
such	O
as	O
papules	O
,	O
vesicles	O
,	O
ulceration	O
and	O
finally	O
scabs	O
over	O
fingers	O
and	O
hands	O
.	O

In	O
camels	O
,	O
the	O
pock-like	O
lesions	O
were	O
distributed	O
over	O
the	O
hairless	O
parts	O
of	O
the	O
body	O
.	O

On	O
the	O
basis	O
of	O
clinical	O
and	O
epidemiological	O
features	O
coupled	O
with	O
serological	O
tests	O
and	O
molecular	O
characterization	O
of	O
the	O
causative	O
agent	O
,	O
CMLV	O
zoonosis	O
was	O
confirmed	O
in	O
3	O
human	O
cases	O
.	O

Clinical	O
samples	O
such	O
as	O
skin	O
scabs/swabs	O
and	O
blood	O
collected	O
from	O
affected	O
animals	O
and	O
humans	O
were	O
analysed	O
initially	O
for	O
the	O
presence	O
of	O
CMLV-specific	O
antigen	O
and	O
antibodies	O
by	O
counter	O

Plague	B-Disease
is	O
a	O

disease	O
in	O
wildlife	O
and	O
is	O
generally	O

to	O

.	O

Humans	O

via	O

direct	O

with	O
infected	O

.	O

Symptoms	O

of	O

,	O

,	O

.	O

,	O

,	O

.	O

in	O

are	O

,	O
